  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414181541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12763069337750276761">I’m as surprised as you are. I’m not sure I believe all of these short finance stories – they sound too good to be true – but this nonfiction piece does motivate me to become a better, fairer person and stop blaming other people for the bad stuff that happens to me. It’s very preachy though, so not for everyone.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_336393408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336393408" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30019-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479137463p2/30019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336393408?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/30019-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=self-improvement-and-spirituality">self-improvement-and-spirituality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=non-fic">non-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336393408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14275030390725494046">Remember The Secret? Oprah made a big thing about it a few years ago, and it become an international bestseller. This book came out in the 1920’s, but makes the same claims. Both are about how your thoughts and words will manifest themselves in your life. If you constantly worry about being hit by a bus, you will manifest yourself into getting hit by a bus. These books claim that the opposite is also true, and can therefore imagine your way to wealth, true love, and happiness.<br/><br/>I started reading T</span>
  <span id="freeText14275030390725494046" style="display:none">Remember The Secret? Oprah made a big thing about it a few years ago, and it become an international bestseller. This book came out in the 1920’s, but makes the same claims. Both are about how your thoughts and words will manifest themselves in your life. If you constantly worry about being hit by a bus, you will manifest yourself into getting hit by a bus. These books claim that the opposite is also true, and can therefore imagine your way to wealth, true love, and happiness.<br /><br />I started reading The Secret back when it was on Oprah and I found it so absurd that I barely made it through ten pages. All it seemed to focus on was material goods, and wealth. People would ask for a pale blue Mustang GT, and because their faith was strong and pure, a pale blue Mustang GT would magically appear in their lives. It felt like a joke, or worse, and infomercial for a cult.<br /><br />The Game of Life is less simplistic, and relies more on the Christian faith to explain why manifestation works (Scovel-Shinn references a lot of Biblical passages). I was actually able to finish it, though I’m not entirely sold on the idea of manifestation. I don’t think you can prevent bad things from happening to you just by having faith, and I don’t think you can have a Mustang GT, in your color of choice, just because you asked for one. Scovel-Shinn never suggests that a bad event can be for the greater good, which is worrisome. No one can live an easy life, no matter how much they pray for one.<br /><br />One good thing that comes from thinking in the way these books suggest is that it probably makes you a happier person. Believing that you will be successful is a lot healthier than believing you’ll be a failure. And sometimes sanity is it’s own reward.<br /><br />There’s a popular saying that says ‘God only gives us what we can handle’. Regardless of whether you believe in God, that point of view makes people stronger and less fearful of troubled waters. So, I’m taking this book with a grain of salt—and choosing to think a lot of happy thoughts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14275030390725494046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3410862906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3410862906" />
    <a title="Bren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61659069-bren"><img alt="Bren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590193281p2/61659069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3410862906?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=educational">educational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=social-issues">social-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=psychology-self-help">psychology-self-help</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=read-and-reviewed">read-and-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=reference">reference</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=better-or-worse-than-expected">better-or-worse-than-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410862906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6939756630093272628">Whatever man feels deeply or images clearly, is impressed upon the subconscious mind, and carried out in minutest detail.<br/><br/>The Game of Life and How to Play It <br/>by Florence Scovel Shinn<br/><br/>I have very, very mixed feelings about this book.<br/><br/>For so many, it seems to fall into love or hate category. For me, it is a bit more complex.<br/><br/>I have never read The Secret, which this book has been compared to. But I will say I did not even expect to finish this. The fact that I did was a surprise to myself.<br/><br/>But I disagre</span>
  <span id="freeText6939756630093272628" style="display:none">Whatever man feels deeply or images clearly, is impressed upon the subconscious mind, and carried out in minutest detail.<br /><br />The Game of Life and How to Play It <br />by Florence Scovel Shinn<br /><br />I have very, very mixed feelings about this book.<br /><br />For so many, it seems to fall into love or hate category. For me, it is a bit more complex.<br /><br />I have never read The Secret, which this book has been compared to. But I will say I did not even expect to finish this. The fact that I did was a surprise to myself.<br /><br />But I disagree with much of it. Although there are things I do agree with.<br /><br />First the good. I can appreciate the power of positive thinking. Many religions and Spiritual theories encourage this. The Buddhists sure do.<br /><br />So does my dad. My dad is a Psychologist and both he and my mom, have specialized in a special kind of therapy called EFT. (Emotional Freedom Therapy).<br /><br />From Wikpedia:<br /><br />Emotional Freedom Techniques (EFT) is a form of counseling intervention that draws on various theories of alternative medicine including acupuncture, neuro-linguistic programming, energy medicine, and Thought Field Therapy (TFT). It is best known through Gary Craig's EFT Handbook, published in the late 1990s, and related books and workshops by a variety of teachers. EFT and similar techniques are often discussed under the umbrella term "energy psychology". <br /><br />EFT is something I have used myself and it relies on purging oneself of negativity and releasing thoughts, beliefs and ideas that hold you back or have you feeling pain.<br /><br />Not really so much different then the theories explained in this book.<br /><br />I do understand and believe in the power of positive thinking and believe it is key. In that regard, I could relate to this book. And positive thinking is something that I have and continue to, struggle mightily with.<br /><br />You have to see it in your mind for it to happen. And for you to believe it will happen. I believe that too and do believe negativity can often be a minefield, bringing forth more and more negativity. I believe that and also believe that forgiveness and healing are imperative..all things that I still struggle with. I d o not want anyone reading this to believe I am this highly enlightened being. The opposite is true. I struggle daily.<br /><br />Here is where I part ways with the book a bit.<br /><br />Although negativity can indeed induce even more negativity and our minds can sometimes make alive our biggest fears, I do not believe that all evil is caused by man alone.<br /><br />This book was written so long ago. It would be interesting to know what the writer,,how they would write it these days.<br /><br />I have some very spiritual friends. We have talks like this constantly. And I will write down what about this book put me off. In other words..what I did not take too.<br /><br />This book would argue that we all have the upper hand in our own life paths. That we are responsible for our own woes, our own love in life, our own illness.<br /><br />QUESTIONS I CANNOT ASK THE WRITER BUT WOULD LIKE TO.<br /><br />How can it be argued that we create all illness? The book says we bring to us that which is inspired by our own thought processes and negativity.<br /><br />What about 9/11?<br /><br />Are we to believe that those who perished brought it to themselves? Of coarse not!<br /><br />What about babies born sick or who die at birth? The book would argue that babies and small children who have illness are ill because of the thoughts of their parents.<br /><br />That makes no sense to me. <br /><br />People who get cancer? People who die in battle? Someone who randomly gets bit by a shark? What about people who are victims of a murderer? And Corona Virus? Is the virus OUR fault ?<br /><br />I could go on a tangent here but you get my drift. I do not subscribe to that belief system. Rather I think bad things happen to good or great people. It is sad that it does but that is what I believe. That life is not always fair.<br /><br />And forgiveness is important. I have many to forgive, including myself.<br /><br />Bu t it is important for the one doing the forgiving.<br /><br />In this book, an example is used of a man who hurts his wife horribly and she is told to forgive him, not to heel herself but because she loves him and her healing will bring him back to her loving arms.<br /><br />I do not want to get all Stepford in this review but it is horribly dangerous thinking, particularly to people like..well..me. And all women honestly.<br /><br />If a woman has the shit kicked out of her and is angry about it? She should send him healing loving thoughts? I think not. I do want to stress that in the example used, the abuse was not psysical. It was psychological but it was still deeply damaging.<br /><br />Do not get me wrong. I believe in forgiveness where once I did not. But that would be to help the person doing the forgiving move on. Not to get the abuser back! I think some of the messages in this book are a bit dated.<br /><br />I believe also that the emphasis on women as home makers shows the book's age. How Feminists would dislike this book! I am not sure if I am a feminist but I did not DISLIKE it. Some of the book's basic messages are true. Positivity DOES attract positivity. But I am not so sure just wishing for a Mercedes will in fact get you one.<br /><br />But hey I am open minded. So right here, I will say I wish for Brad Pitt. Hey, he's single again. I wish for Brad Pitt to ask me for a date. Let's see what happens!<br /><br />In all seriousness..sometimes the message..or parts of it..can be right but go a bit far out and that is basically what I think of the book. I'd say it is a quick and interesting read and go ahead and read it! Much to debate in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6939756630093272628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1921855023" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16656754667124836782">A fantastic summary of some essential principles. <br/><br/>Excerpts :<br/>-----------<br/><br/>“The imaging faculty plays a leading part in the game of life.  … What man images, sooner or later, externalizes in his affairs.”<br/><br/>“Fear must be erased from the consciousness… We must substitute fear with faith, for fear is only inverted faith. It is faith in evil, instead of good... Fear is misdirected energy which must be redirected - or transmuted - into faith.”<br/><br/>“The object of the game of life is to seek clearly one’s good an</span>
  <span id="freeText16656754667124836782" style="display:none">A fantastic summary of some essential principles. <br /><br />Excerpts :<br />-----------<br /><br />“The imaging faculty plays a leading part in the game of life.  … What man images, sooner or later, externalizes in his affairs.”<br /><br />“Fear must be erased from the consciousness… We must substitute fear with faith, for fear is only inverted faith. It is faith in evil, instead of good... Fear is misdirected energy which must be redirected - or transmuted - into faith.”<br /><br />“The object of the game of life is to seek clearly one’s good and obliterate all pictures of evil.”<br /><br />“Why worry? It will probably never happen.”<br /><br />“There is a supply for every demand.”<br /><br />“Your job is to act rich, thereby showing perfect faith that you will receive it…”<br /><br />“Speak these words aloud with power and conviction : 'I now smash and demolish by my spoken word every untrue record in my subconscious mind. They shall return to the dustheap of their native nothingness, for they came from my own vain imaginings. I now make my perfect records from the Christ within : the records of health, wealth, love, and perfect self-expression.' ”<br /><br />“Death and life are in the power of the tongue.” (Proverbs 18:21)<br /><br />“If one asks for success, and is prepared for failure, he will get the situation he prepared for.”<br /><br />“Man must prepare for the thing he asked for when there isn’t the slightest sign of it in sight.”<br /><br />“Before ye call, I shall answer.” (Isaiah 65:24)<br /><br />“Every great work, every big accomplishment has been brought into manifestation through holding to the vision.”<br /><br />“...You lost your temper at the bank, and therefore your power."<br /><br />“A person should not hesitate to ask for help if he sees himself wavering.”<br /><br />“No man can fail if some one person sees him as successful. Such is the power of the vision, and many a great man has owed his success to a wife or a sister or a friend who believed in him and held without wavering to the perfect pattern.”<br /><br />“The horseshoe or rabbit’s foot contains no power but man’s spoken word and belief that it will bring him good luck. It creates expectancy in the subconscious…”<br /><br />“The forces are always working for the man who is pulling the strings himself, although he does not know it.”<br /><br />“This so often happens: If one is willing to do a thing he is afraid to do, he does not have to. It is the law of non-resistance... Courage contains genius and magic. Face a situation fearlessly, and there is no situation to face. It falls away of its own weight.”<br /><br />“Talk about what we want, not about what we don’t want.”<br /><br />“There is an old saying: that man only dares to use his words for 3 purposes : to heal, bless, or prosper. What man says of others will be said of him, and what he wishes for another he is wishing for himself.”<br /><br />“The body may be renewed and transformed through the spoken word and clear vision... In order to heal the body, one must first heal the soul. The soul is the subconscious mind, and it must be saved from wrong thinking.”<br /><br />“Love and good will destroy the enemies within oneself, therefore one has no enemies on the external.”<br /><br />“Nothing on earth can resist an absolutely nonresistant person. The Chinese say water is the most powerful element, because it is perfectly nonresistant... Christ said 'Resist not evil', because he knew in reality there was no evil, so there was nothing to resist... So long as man resists a situation, he will have it with him. If he runs away from it, it will run after him.”<br /><br />“If you do not run your subconscious mind yourself, someone else will run it for you.”<br /><br />“Every man is a golden link in the chain of my good, for all men are God in manifestation.”<br /><br />“One’s ships come in over a calm sea.”<br /><br />“Man should watch himself hourly to detect if his action is fear or faith.”<br /><br />“Living in the past is a failure method, and a violation of spiritual law. Jesus Christ said 'Behold! Now is the accepted time. Now is the day of salvation.' ”<br /><br />“Make an affirmation immediately upon waking… I have wonderful work, and a wonderful way. I give wonderful service for wonderful pay.”<br /><br />“One of my students asked me to explain the darkness before the dawn… ‘How long must one remain in the dark?’ And I replied ‘Until one can see in the dark.’ ”<br /><br />“Faith without work is dead.”<br /><br />“Before Columbus reached America, he saw birds with twigs to show him land was near.”<br /><br />“Be in a rapturous state of mind… without envying others.”<br /><br />“Why are ye fearful, oh ye of little faith! All things are possible to him that believeth.” - Christ<br /><br />“God is the giver and the gift… As one is one with the giver, he is one with the gift… He must be in harmony with the thing in order to attract it."<br /><br />“Love is God in manifestation, and the strongest magnetic force in the universe. Pure, unselfish love draws to itself its own.”<br /><br />“Money is God in manifestation, as freedom from want and limitation. But it must always be kept in circulation, put to right uses.”<br /><br />“Christ knew that all sickness came from sin, but admonished the leper after the healing.”<br /><br />“Man picks up a live wire whenever he criticizes or condemns, and may pick up a shock.”<br /><br />“Make this statement repeatedly: ‘I am always under direct inspiration. I make right decisions, quickly.’ These words impress the subconscious, and soon one finds himself awake and alert, making his right moves without hesitation.”<br /><br />“I have found it destructive to look to the psychic plane for guidance, as it is the plane of many minds, and not the One Mind. As man opens his mind to subjectivity, he becomes a target for destructive forces.”<br /><br />“Wisdom’s ways are ways of pleasantness, and all her paths are peace.”<br /><br />“Poise is power, for it gives God-power a chance to rush through man, to will and to do its good… Poised, he thinks clearly, and makes right decisions quickly. He never misses a trick.”<br /><br />“Fear and worry are sins… Man is God, afraid.”<br /><br />“Make this statement : ‘In divine mind, there is only completion…’ Perhaps you are in the habit of leaving things unfinished?” <br /><br />“Suppose one has several talents. How is he to choose? Make the statement ‘I am fully equipped for the divine plan of my life’ and be fearless in grasping opportunities.” <br /><br />“Man goes through many lives and deaths, until he knows the truth which sets him free. He is drawn back to the earth-plane through unsatisfied desires, to pay his karmic debts or to fulfill his destiny.”<br /><br /><br />...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7807592426701382866">“The game of life is a game of boomerangs. Our thoughts, deeds and words return to us sooner or later with astounding accuracy.” This quote practically sums up the purpose of the book. Although Shinn uses a lot of biblical references to prove her arguments, I believe that her philosophies can be applied to all people with different faiths. She uses a lot of real life examples to prove her points which I loved since most people can relate to the examples she referred to. <br/><br/>Shinn mentions that throu</span>
  <span id="freeText7807592426701382866" style="display:none">“The game of life is a game of boomerangs. Our thoughts, deeds and words return to us sooner or later with astounding accuracy.” This quote practically sums up the purpose of the book. Although Shinn uses a lot of biblical references to prove her arguments, I believe that her philosophies can be applied to all people with different faiths. She uses a lot of real life examples to prove her points which I loved since most people can relate to the examples she referred to. <br /><br />Shinn mentions that through the correct frame of mind and intention, one can get the key to a happy life and it is god’s intentions to give him that life. I particularly liked it when she discussed that every human being in this world is great at doing something, and that thing is his destiny that God wants him to pursue in life. <br /><br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who seriously wants to change their outlook about life. In my opinion, Shinn successfully communicates in her book that the power of changing our lives is within us.<br /></span>

<div id="review_686516229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686516229" />
    <a title="Jo Ledamun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21885802-jo-ledamun"><img alt="Jo Ledamun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372892308p2/21885802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686516229?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Ledamun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Ledamun" href="/user/show/21885802-jo-ledamun">Jo Ledamun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686516229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4348271035225387584">What a load of old tosh!<br/><br/>I know many people may disagree & I DO NOT MEAN TO INSULT, but.......<br/><br/>I did not like this book at all - admittedly I was a bit skeptical about it from the beginning, but I wanted to give it a go, so I gave it my best shot!<br/><br/>The 3 best things about this book is that it's short and sweet, well written & the authors viewpoint/argument is easy to comprehend! But in MY OPINION, I think what Florence Scovel-Shinn suggests & argues about in her book about wealth, happiness, health,</span>
  <span id="freeText4348271035225387584" style="display:none">What a load of old tosh!<br /><br />I know many people may disagree &amp; I DO NOT MEAN TO INSULT, but.......<br /><br />I did not like this book at all - admittedly I was a bit skeptical about it from the beginning, but I wanted to give it a go, so I gave it my best shot!<br /><br />The 3 best things about this book is that it's short and sweet, well written &amp; the authors viewpoint/argument is easy to comprehend! But in MY OPINION, I think what Florence Scovel-Shinn suggests &amp; argues about in her book about wealth, happiness, health, love &amp; success; is mostly a whole load of old tosh!<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I am not anti:<br />People wanting to achieve the most out of life or them wanting the same for others<br />Wanting to be happy<br />Christian values<br />Or<br />Positive thinking.<br /><br />But I think for some people 'a good boot up the bottom' or 'reality check' would be more prudent to them, than them believing in affirmations or practising Scovel-Shinn's methodologies.<br /><br />Instead of practising the methodologies suggested, if people want to try and achieve a particular goal or overcome a personal issue, I think it would be more beneficial for them; to adopt a more proactive &amp; practical approach. For example, different types of experiential learning might be one possibility? Such as Kolb (1984) or Honey &amp; Mumford (1982).<br /><br />Guess what? After reading this book, I have no intention or desire anytime soon to read 'The Secret' by Rhonda Byrne; but who knows, 'never say never'!<br /><br />If you read this book, I hope you enjoy it, far more than I did &amp; you benefit from reading it?<br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_109242021" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109242021" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/613016-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194733122p2/613016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109242021?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/613016-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789568356170" href="/book/show/2261575.The_Game_of_Life_and_How_to_Play_It">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/613016-maggie?shelf=secular-inspirational">secular-inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109242021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15913929997431684855">at first blush, i didn't like this book b/c i totally do not agree with the "manifestation" belief system so prevalent today. it is a very small god, made in our own self-serving image, who can be made to do the bidding of our petty desires: the gimmee-gimmee god.<br/><br/>however, i do believe in grace and in being open to grace and goodness; and i certainly believe in right behavior, esp. as zen buddhism defines it. <br/><br/>this book, on first blush, seemed to focus totally on the power of an individual -- thro</span>
  <span id="freeText15913929997431684855" style="display:none">at first blush, i didn't like this book b/c i totally do not agree with the "manifestation" belief system so prevalent today. it is a very small god, made in our own self-serving image, who can be made to do the bidding of our petty desires: the gimmee-gimmee god.<br /><br />however, i do believe in grace and in being open to grace and goodness; and i certainly believe in right behavior, esp. as zen buddhism defines it. <br /><br />this book, on first blush, seemed to focus totally on the power of an individual -- through thoughts, words, and actions -- to manifest good things in their life ... and of course the not-so-good things that happen in everyone's life, which is where i really object to manifestation's big-gumball-machine-in-the-sky concept. people get sick and don't bring it on themselves; people have good fortune and don't do a single thing to bring it on or for that matter even to deserve it. case closed.<br /><br />so, imo, manifestation is not right-thinking as zen buddhism defines right thinking. even as i do NOT believe in "manifestation" i certainly DO believe in coincidence, i.e. G-d choosing to remain anonymous. things happen -- good and not quite so good -- and it behooves us to pay attention. so i suppose i believe in attention far more than i believe in "manifestation", which is far more nuanced than mere mortals are capable of understanding.<br /><br />however i decided to stay with the book until at least the 3rd and 4th chapters and slowly -- very slowly -- began to recognize <i>some</i> valid points. helpful and almost healthy thoughts, actually. so <b>IF</b> a person reads this work with a critical mind that knows how to separate the wheat from the chaff, then that reader could possibly refine their thoughts on what life's game is about and how best to be a player. but beware of her definitions. not all of them are reliable.<br /><br /><i>test everything; retain what is good</i> 1 thessalonians 5:21<br /><br />or another favorite: <i>be shrewd as serpents and simple as doves</i> matthew 10: 16<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15913929997431684855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13903276182737972642" style="display:none"><b> Updated October 22, 2019 </b><br />I read this book three years ago and I remember being impressed by how simply the writing was and the lasting impression it made on me. I love being reminded how my words have power and I need to focus and pay attention to the things I speak into my life and the lives of others. I also loved the affirmations and I am looking to incorporate them into my daily life. <br />A short but effective read.<br /><br /><b> 2016 </b> <br />Someone recommended I read this book after I told them about "The Monk Who Sold His Ferrari". I loved that this book also made reference to various Bible verses because all of these "new age" thinking are deeply rooted in the Bible. <br />I love the daily affirmations, a sense of calm and peace over comes me after saying the applicable ones. <br />A great read. I will definitely be re-reading this.</span>

  <span id="freeText13964310791566352493" style="display:none">I learnt nothing from this book!<br /><br />Firstly, I have no doubt in positive thinking, but it's not all about positive thoughts. We can't just "ask god" for things and expect to have them all, because life is hard and it can be unfair sometimes. We should accept the fact that the rosy world doesn't exist. So if we want something we have to WORK in order to have it, not sitting and hoping that the thing we are asking for is going to be right in front of us.<br /><br />I believe that I have to move forward and be strong after breakup, not waiting and praying that my ex is going to change his mind and come back (like the woman who waited her husband after he left her and went with another woman).<br />And one last thing, I MAY forgive people who hurt me in the past, but I will never "bless them"!!<br />So yes, this was the worst book I've ever read.</span>

<div id="review_437686652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437686652" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13658847-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437686652?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/13658847-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437686652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14955652200352126527">If Rhonda Byrne's THE SECRET had been written with a Christian bent, in a primarily Christian age and culture like the 20's, and contained only author anecdotes about people rather than by the people themselves, you would have this book: THE GAME OF LIFE AND HOW TO PLAY IT. <br/><br/>The author, Florence Scovel-Shinn, centers her book on the basic premise of the "law of attraction," which is also set forth by other famous authors/presenters such as Ester and Jerry Hicks. The idea, supported by many exampl</span>
  <span id="freeText14955652200352126527" style="display:none">If Rhonda Byrne's THE SECRET had been written with a Christian bent, in a primarily Christian age and culture like the 20's, and contained only author anecdotes about people rather than by the people themselves, you would have this book: THE GAME OF LIFE AND HOW TO PLAY IT. <br /><br />The author, Florence Scovel-Shinn, centers her book on the basic premise of the "law of attraction," which is also set forth by other famous authors/presenters such as Ester and Jerry Hicks. The idea, supported by many examples in the book, is that that you attract what you concentrate upon. And if you accept that, then you had better start concentrating upon things you really want. Otherwise, you will let your focus drift more toward your worries, doubts and fears - and then you'll manifest those things in your life simply because you're thinking about them. I find this to be a necessary reminder in my life, since I lapse into the habit of worry and anxious thinking by default. I have used this reminder to "manifest" a better suited job, to worry less, and generally to make better everyday and major life decisions. <br /><br />What I did not like is that both books focus on the monetary aspect of getting what you want, probably because nothing has changed in the nearly 100 years since GAME OF LIFE was written. People want money, have always wanted money, and always will want more money. It's a little disconcerting, actually, knowing that this hasn't changed at all. But many of the examples - those that I choose to concentrate upon - involve creating health and happiness in one's life. I also learned great ways to formulate affirmations, which is apparently one of Scovel-Shinn's known specialities. For example, to create more free time in my life, I asked to receive opportunities for this "under grace" - otherwise, opportunities for free time might be created under adverse circumstances like losing health or a job. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14955652200352126527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_373907150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373907150" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/827562-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437764861p2/827562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373907150?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/827562-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780875167824" href="/book/show/198914.The_Game_of_Life_for_Women_and_How_to_Play_It">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/827562-christine?shelf=business">business</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/827562-christine?shelf=motivational">motivational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/827562-christine?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/827562-christine?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373907150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17453400393824820727"><br/> [This is an alternate version of an existing book; see my review of "The Game of Life and How to Play It."]<br/><br/> MY STARS..<br/>..number 4 out of 5.<br/><br/>"The Game of Life for Women" has just about the same content as Ms. Shinn's original "The Game of Life and How to Play It"; but "For Women" gets one less star from me specifically for its translation into entirely feminine pronouns. <br/><br/>I can understand publishing a version in which non-gender-specific references are represented with feminine pronouns, rather tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17453400393824820727" style="display:none"><br /> [This is an alternate version of an existing book; see my review of "The Game of Life and How to Play It."]<br /><br /> MY STARS..<br />..number 4 out of 5.<br /><br />"The Game of Life for Women" has just about the same content as Ms. Shinn's original "The Game of Life and How to Play It"; but "For Women" gets one less star from me specifically for its translation into entirely feminine pronouns. <br /><br />I can understand publishing a version in which non-gender-specific references are represented with feminine pronouns, rather than the all-masculine pronouns commonly used in the formal grammar of Ms. Shinn's early-20th-century day; but this version goes a step further and transforms ALL male references to female--even when the anecdote was originally about a man.<br /><br />I think this wasn't the best idea, for two reasons:<br /><br />1: You'd be hard-put to find a woman on Earth who doesn't have SOME males in her life. An all-female existence feels unnatural in the anecdotes, and distracts me from the core purpose of the book. Ms. Shinn's original version had no shortage of stories about female clients &amp; friends--as a matter of fact, all her books contain pretty much an equal balance of guys &amp; gals. Better to have converted general pronouns to the feminine to achieve the "for women" effect, and leave the subjects of Ms. Shinn's stories alone.<br /><br />2: Suddenly her book is awash in female chauvinists. :) In Ms. Shinn's original stories, it's always fun to see her stand her ground against pompous patriarchs who are inclined to discredit the advice of a mere woman. Her good sense &amp; faith in God always win the day; but that effect is diminished in this femininized version.<br /><br />LET ME SUM-UP:<br /><br />If you're a female reader who'd feel more comfortable with a book that frames its advice specifically for women, then this is a good choice for you. I go to it myself when I just don't feel up to fighting old pronouns.<br /><br />However, I'd also encourage you to read the original "Game of Life" in Ms. Shinn's own words. Because much is lost in the translation; and I know you're confident enough in your own identity not to be offended by great-grandma's grammar. :)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17453400393824820727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16520324120057571938">Florence wrote her book in 1925 and I didn't know how lucid or practical the book would be and I was indeed in for a lovely surprise. The book reads so well, easily understood, lucid in style, practical and applicable in every way. It feels as if a compassionate mother is sitting with me and taking me by the hand and instructing me in order to apply my faith. Most important lesson Momma Florence has taught me is that God is my supply, and there is a supply for every demand. I have to confess tha</span>
  <span id="freeText16520324120057571938" style="display:none">Florence wrote her book in 1925 and I didn't know how lucid or practical the book would be and I was indeed in for a lovely surprise. The book reads so well, easily understood, lucid in style, practical and applicable in every way. It feels as if a compassionate mother is sitting with me and taking me by the hand and instructing me in order to apply my faith. Most important lesson Momma Florence has taught me is that God is my supply, and there is a supply for every demand. I have to confess that and affirm it daily. If I don't speak the word, how in the world am I gonna receive? Our Lord commands me to "ask" before I can receive. And how do I ask? I must act as if I had already received. That is believing asking and it takes place in an atmosphere of thanksgiving and gratitude. I should not focus on circumstances, thus giving them power. Instead, I should see myself as God sees me, an honorable child of His. Because I have faith in how the Lord works, I am choosing not to be disturbed by circumstances, by what "appears". Don't ever make giant out of circumstances! Focus on your Divine supply. Recently I have been contemplating Psalm 23 in what it says "He restores me", that is, He renews my life. I have to affirm that also. I unite myself to God's Divine Mind. His will be done in my life. What does that mean? It means Divine order is established in my mind, body and affairs. Your will be done in my life, dear Lord, as You and I are one, and I unite myself with your Divine purpose and will. Your Love cleanses my entire being now. The Love of God abolishes anything contrary to Love in my life. Your Love dissolves anything unlike love. I am going to devote each day as I wake up to the Lord. I will affirm: Today is a day of completion; I give thanks for this perfect day, and I believe miracles shall flow and wonders shall never cease. <br />Towards the end, the last chapter has a summary of beautiful affirmations that will come handy for different uses. This book is a gem and sheer delight. You could read it online here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sacred-texts.com/nth/shinn/gol/index.htm">http://www.sacred-texts.com/nth/shinn...</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trixy Lemell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trixy Lemell" href="/user/show/7155945-trixy-lemell">Trixy Lemell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408185506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer854704023932403448">I really can't give this book a high rating or recommend it to anyone. It would just be irresponsible. I am all for the whole idea of believing and visualizing and affirmations to make things come to be but this is just way over the top for me. <br/><br/>This idea that if your baby dies or becomes ill it is because you brought it on due to not wanting them to become ill. Can't get behind that. People do not wish cancer onto themselves or their loved ones. At the same time you can't just visualize and reci</span>
  <span id="freeText854704023932403448" style="display:none">I really can't give this book a high rating or recommend it to anyone. It would just be irresponsible. I am all for the whole idea of believing and visualizing and affirmations to make things come to be but this is just way over the top for me. <br /><br />This idea that if your baby dies or becomes ill it is because you brought it on due to not wanting them to become ill. Can't get behind that. People do not wish cancer onto themselves or their loved ones. At the same time you can't just visualize and recite affirmations and cancer just poofs away. You can't live in Tornado city and recite some affirmations and poof away all of the tornados. You wanting a new house does not cause someone else to die for your wants. If they do die that is not your fault. There are many of people who knew that one person who recited their own prayers and the such. <br /><br />People aren't always bright. I'm just afraid that someone will read this and decide that they don't need to take their 3 year old in for cancer treatments or to the dentist for a tooth cleaning. <br /><br />And this thing against saving money? The story about the woman who saved up for a holiday meal and had it stolen and that was her fault because instead of saving she should have spent it all and God would have given her the money in the end. Nope. <br /><br />There are millions of people around the world who suffer and pray and are devoted and still suffer. God kills them and their children and spouses and family even though all of the above are praying and practicing just as this book says. <br /><br />I'm fine with positive thinking and visualization. I'm fine with gratitude. I draw the line with blaming parents for the death of their children and blaming victims of crimes, mother nature, and disease for what has happened to them. Yes, it is up to them to react to those things in a different way but the fact that so and so was raped is not because they brought it upon themselves because they forgot a line in a prayer or were worried about walking through that dark parking lot alone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="854704023932403448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736133964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11743426174989034334">I read the 2012 edition of this book, edited by Ruth Miller and it had a lot of updates to the original text and new citations to support the ideas. The original text was published at the back of the book. I gave this book three stars because without the modern update, I don't think I would have connected with it as much. To be fair, it was originally published in the 1920's so it's easy to see how things have changed a bit between now and then. Read the new edition, if you have the chance. I en</span>
  <span id="freeText11743426174989034334" style="display:none">I read the 2012 edition of this book, edited by Ruth Miller and it had a lot of updates to the original text and new citations to support the ideas. The original text was published at the back of the book. I gave this book three stars because without the modern update, I don't think I would have connected with it as much. To be fair, it was originally published in the 1920's so it's easy to see how things have changed a bit between now and then. Read the new edition, if you have the chance. I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The most helpful part of this book to me was the idea of giving over "control" of the idea of your ultimate best or greatest good to the universal mind (who theoretically at least, has better ideas than you being and knowing all as it does). I think too often, people get stuck visioning life one way, their way, and forget that something even better might be out there if they could just see it. Shinn suggests wording your affirmations and prayers to include the phrase "to the divine plan" or "by divine right". She provides countless stories of people who tried to run their life by their plan and it turned out pretty badly. Faith and trust in a benevolent and loving universe are central ideas to her book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11743426174989034334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13804063486935902761" style="display:none">The best thing about the book for me was the way by chance it came in the suggested YouTube videos, of which I loved the title.<br />I then discovered how it was written about a century ago, and I admired the point of view of the writer in describing the spiritual laws (or metaphysical laws) and their influence on our lives. Also in that free YouTube audiobook the voice of the reader and the style is in perfect harmony with the book, that I thought it is read by the author.<br />Understanding these spiritual laws and their application on our lives will change a lot for everyone who believes in them.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4151550008394817905">How long must one remain in the dark?<br/>Until one can see in the dark. <br/>The Game of Life and How to Play It is a good enough new age manifestation book. There are places which are striking and make sense. But there is also too much simplification that makes manifestation look less like a science. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VxLuwdslPVSQfrcdVriJ4IIauKGH15frpuaQgSM79trQYTO8vZ758Jc2azi7aJk4f8rAme9+ZcpgvUTRv8HaDQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eSH5hvx6Te/2i1Rdf/vqFWf6bcOJ66312l4tQXarxOb+UiT7msGJS/HDiHiSK/rNmioV++FCX9QcBfkR6lHoMQ==')})
  }
